# DUAL INDEPENDENT AUDIT — I-meta-008 #1034: thin oa_full_text stub blocks OpenAlex fallback

You are one of TWO independent auditors (Claude + Codex) running in parallel per the
POLARIS §-1.1 line-by-line standard. Audit claim-by-claim against the actual code + the
run-6 evidence. Do NOT rubber-stamp. Surface every real finding.

## The change under review (v2 fix, committed)
`src/polaris_graph/retrieval/frame_fetcher.py` + tests. The diff is in
`.codex/I-meta-008-thinstub/codex_diff.patch`.

Summary of the v2 logic:
- New `_OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS` (default 1200). An OA full-text fetch shorter than this is
  treated as a STUB, not real full text.
- Step 4 OpenAlex fallback now fires when `not abstract_crossref and not abstract_pubmed
  and (not oa_full_text or len(oa_full_text) < _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS)`.
- `_pick_richest_abstract(crossref, openalex, pubmed, partial_full_text)` chooses the
  LONGEST text; ties keep priority order (CrossRef > OpenAlex > PubMed > thin-partial).
- Decision: real full text (>= threshold) wins; else the richest abstract; a 540-char
  stub loses to a 1331-char OpenAlex abstract. Provenance OPEN_ACCESS if an OA locator
  existed, else ABSTRACT_ONLY.

## The diagnosis to verify (run-6 evidence in run6_frame_evidence.txt)
Claim: in run 6, `acemoglu_restrepo_automation_tasks` (the foundational "Automation and
New Tasks" JEP paper, DOI 10.1257/jep.33.2.3) came back provenance=open_access with
oa_full_text PRESENT but crossref_abstract ABSENT — i.e. the aeaweb PDF 403'd and Jina
returned a ~540-char STUB that was used as direct_quote, which the generator could not
extract fields from -> "not extractable". The old #1033 fallback was blocked because
oa_full_text was truthy. OpenAlex holds the real 1331-char abstract.

## What I need you to independently audit (line-by-line)
1. **Diff correctness**: is `_pick_richest_abstract` deterministic? (ties -> priority via
   strictly-greater while iterating; positions of equal length.) Any off-by-one / wrong
   branch / wrong provenance label?
2. **Threshold logic**: does the v2 change correctly let OpenAlex fire on a thin stub
   while still preferring a real long full text? Is 1200 a defensible boundary (a real
   full-text extraction is much longer; a paywall stub is ~540)? Any case where a
   legitimately short-but-real abstract is mishandled?
3. **Does v2 actually fix run-6's failures?** Walk EACH of the 7 entities in
   run6_frame_evidence.txt and state whether v2 grounds it, and with which source:
   - acemoglu_automation (oa_full_text stub, no crossref): does OpenAlex now fire + win?
   - acemoglu_robots (metadata_only): helped by #1033 already?
   - autor / frey_osborne (oa_full_text present, got real content run-6): unchanged?
   - brynjolfsson / eloundou (crossref_abstract present): NOT helped by OpenAlex — is that
     an honest residual (the effect number isn't in the abstract / generator-extraction
     issue), or does the diff need to also fire OpenAlex when crossref abstract is thin?
4. **Any OTHER bug** in the fetch path exposed by this change (determinism, the DOI guard,
   network discipline, the provenance downgrade when any_oa_url but empty quote)?
5. **Regression risk**: existing M-66b-T test uses full_text ~1650 chars (>=1200 -> still
   real full text). Confirm no existing behavior breaks.

+    """Choose the RICHEST (longest) available abstract text + its
+    quote_source label. Candidates in priority order CrossRef >
+    OpenAlex > PubMed > thin-OA-full-text partial; the LONGEST wins,
+    ties break toward the higher-priority source (deterministic —
+    strictly-greater comparison while iterating priority order).
+
+    A thin oa_full_text stub (paywalled-PDF Jina result, ~540 chars)
+    is admitted only as the last-priority `partial_full_text`
+    candidate, so a real abstract (e.g. OpenAlex 1331 chars) overrides
+    it rather than being blocked by it (issue #1034). Returns
+    ("", "none") when every candidate is empty."""

+        candidates.append((openalex, "openalex_abstract"))
+    if pubmed:
+        candidates.append((pubmed, "pubmed_abstract"))
+    if partial_full_text:
+        candidates.append((partial_full_text, "oa_full_text_partial"))
+    best: tuple[str, str] | None = None
+    for text, src in candidates:
+        if best is None or len(text) > len(best[0]):
+            best = (text, src)
+    return best if best is not None else ("", "none")

+class TestOpenAlexThinStubRichest:
+    def test_pick_richest_longest_wins_ties_keep_priority(self) -> None:
+        from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.frame_fetcher import (

+        # OpenAlex longest -> wins despite CrossRef higher priority.

+            crossref="short", openalex="x" * 50, pubmed=None,
+        )
+        assert s == "openalex_abstract" and t == "x" * 50
+        # Equal length -> CrossRef (higher priority) wins.
+        t, s = _pick_richest_abstract(
+            crossref="abcd", openalex="wxyz", pubmed=None,
+        )
+        assert s == "crossref_abstract"
+        # Only a thin partial full-text present -> it is used last-resort.
+        t, s = _pick_richest_abstract(
+            crossref=None, openalex=None, pubmed=None,

+            crossref=None, openalex=None, pubmed=None,
+        ) == ("", "none")
+
+    def test_thin_oa_fulltext_stub_does_not_block_openalex(
+        self, monkeypatch: pytest.MonkeyPatch
+    ) -> None:
+        """THE #1034 BUG: aeaweb PDF 403s but Jina returns a ~540-char
+        stub. The stub must NOT block OpenAlex; the richer OpenAlex
+        abstract (>=1200) must win, not the stub."""
+        stub = "X" * 540  # below _OA_FULLTEXT_MIN_CHARS (1200)
+        monkeypatch.setattr(
+            "src.polaris_graph.retrieval.frame_fetcher._fetch_url_pattern",
+            lambda url: (stub, url),
+        )
+        cr_no_abs = _crossref_response(abstract=None)
+        transport = _Transport([
+            ("api.crossref.org", 200, cr_no_abs),
+            ("api.unpaywall.org", 200, _unpaywall_response(
+                is_oa=True,
+                pdf_url="https://www.aeaweb.org/articles/pdf/x.pdf")),
+            ("api.openalex.org", 200,
+             _openalex_response(sentence=_LONG_OPENALEX_SENTENCE)),
+        ])
+        with _client_with_transport(transport) as client:
+            row = fetch_frame_entity(
+                _binding(
+                    primary="doi:10.1056/NEJMoa2107519", secondaries=()
+                ),
+                client=client,
+            )
+        assert row.provenance_class == ProvenanceClass.OPEN_ACCESS
+        assert row.quote_source == "openalex_abstract"  # NOT the stub
+        assert "finding200" in row.direct_quote
+        assert "XXXX" not in row.direct_quote  # the stub did not win
+        assert len(row.direct_quote) > 540
+        assert any(
+            "openalex" in a.source for a in row.retrieval_attempts
+        )
+
+    def test_real_long_fulltext_still_preferred_over_openalex(

+    ) -> None:

  739: def _call_openalex(
  740:     client: httpx.Client, doi: str
  741: ) -> tuple[dict[str, Any] | None, list[RetrievalAttempt], list[RetrievalTiming]]:
  742:     """Deterministic OpenAlex /works/{doi} fetch (issue #1033).
  743: 
  744:     Abstract fallback for journal DOIs where CrossRef returned no
  745:     abstract and the OA full-text PDF was paywalled (403). Uses the
  746:     same retry/attempt-logging discipline as the other callers so
  747:     M-60 manifest telemetry shows the OpenAlex attempt."""
  748:     email = os.getenv("PG_UNPAYWALL_EMAIL", "polaris@example.org")
  749:     url = _OPENALEX_WORK_BASE + "https://doi.org/" + _urlsafe_doi(doi)
  750:     r, outcome, attempts, timings = _request_with_retry(
  751:         client, "GET", "openalex", url, params={"mailto": email},
  752:     )
  753:     if outcome != "success" or r is None:
  754:         return None, attempts, timings
  755:     try:
  756:         data = r.json()
  757:     except ValueError:
  758:         last = attempts[-1]
  759:         attempts[-1] = RetrievalAttempt(
  760:             source=last.source, url=last.url,
  761:             attempt_index=last.attempt_index,
  762:             http_status=last.http_status,
  763:             outcome="error:invalid_json",
  764:         )
  765:         return None, attempts, timings
  766:     return data, attempts, timings

  768: 
  769: def _pick_richest_abstract(
  770:     *,
  771:     crossref: str | None,
  772:     openalex: str | None,
  773:     pubmed: str | None,
  774:     partial_full_text: str | None = None,
  775: ) -> tuple[str, str]:
  776:     """Choose the RICHEST (longest) available abstract text + its
  777:     quote_source label. Candidates in priority order CrossRef >
  778:     OpenAlex > PubMed > thin-OA-full-text partial; the LONGEST wins,
  779:     ties break toward the higher-priority source (deterministic —
  780:     strictly-greater comparison while iterating priority order).
  781: 
  782:     A thin oa_full_text stub (paywalled-PDF Jina result, ~540 chars)
  783:     is admitted only as the last-priority `partial_full_text`
  784:     candidate, so a real abstract (e.g. OpenAlex 1331 chars) overrides
  785:     it rather than being blocked by it (issue #1034). Returns
  786:     ("", "none") when every candidate is empty."""
  787:     candidates: list[tuple[str, str]] = []
  788:     if crossref:
  789:         candidates.append((crossref, "crossref_abstract"))
  790:     if openalex:
  791:         candidates.append((openalex, "openalex_abstract"))
  792:     if pubmed:
  793:         candidates.append((pubmed, "pubmed_abstract"))
  794:     if partial_full_text:
  795:         candidates.append((partial_full_text, "oa_full_text_partial"))
  796:     best: tuple[str, str] | None = None
  797:     for text, src in candidates:
  798:         if best is None or len(text) > len(best[0]):
  799:             best = (text, src)
  800:     return best if best is not None else ("", "none")
  801: 
  802: 
  803: def _urlsafe_doi(doi: str) -> str:
  804:     """CrossRef and Unpaywall accept DOIs verbatim; percent-encode
  805:     any slashes? The standard is to pass the raw DOI. Both APIs
  806:     accept both forms. We keep it raw — no encoding needed for the
  807:     typical DOI characters (10.XXXX/YYYY)."""
  808:     return doi.strip()

  379: 
  380: def _reconstruct_inverted_abstract(inverted_index: Any) -> str | None:
  381:     """Reconstruct a plain-text abstract from an OpenAlex
  382:     `abstract_inverted_index` ({word: [pos, ...]}). Deterministic:
  383:     positions are unique within a work, so sort-by-position is a
  384:     total order -> same input yields byte-identical text.
  385: 
  386:     Kept local (mirrors the proven reconstruction in
  387:     agents/searcher.py) so frame_fetcher stays free of the
  388:     non-deterministic keyword-retrieval stack per its module
  389:     determinism contract."""
  390:     if not isinstance(inverted_index, dict) or not inverted_index:
  391:         return None
  392:     word_positions: list[tuple[int, str]] = []
  393:     for word, positions in inverted_index.items():
  394:         if not isinstance(positions, (list, tuple)):
  395:             continue
  396:         for pos in positions:
  397:             if isinstance(pos, int):
  398:                 word_positions.append((pos, word))
  399:     if not word_positions:
  400:         return None
  401:     word_positions.sort()
  402:     text = " ".join(w for _, w in word_positions).strip()
  403:     return text or None
  404: 
  405: 
  406: def _parse_openalex_response(data: dict[str, Any]) -> dict[str, Any]:
  407:     """Extract abstract + metadata from an OpenAlex /works/{doi}
  408:     JSON object (issue #1033). Abstract is reconstructed from
  409:     abstract_inverted_index. Returns dict with keys: title, authors,
  410:     journal, year, abstract, doi (normalized, prefix-stripped,
  411:     lowercased). Values may be None/empty when absent."""
  412:     if not isinstance(data, dict):
  413:         return {}
  414:     abstract = _reconstruct_inverted_abstract(
  415:         data.get("abstract_inverted_index")
  416:     )
  417: 
  418:     title = data.get("title") or data.get("display_name") or None
  419:     if isinstance(title, str):
  420:         title = title.strip() or None
  421: 
  422:     authors: list[str] = []
  423:     for a in (data.get("authorships") or []):
  424:         if not isinstance(a, dict):
  425:             continue
  426:         au = a.get("author")
  427:         name = (au.get("display_name") or "").strip() if isinstance(au, dict) else ""
  428:         if name:
  429:             authors.append(name)
  430: 
  431:     journal = None

 1152: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 1153: # (8) OpenAlex abstract fallback (issue #1033)
 1154: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
 1155: def _openalex_response(
 1156:     *,
 1157:     doi: str = "10.1056/NEJMoa2107519",
 1158:     sentence: str = "Tirzepatide reduced HbA1c substantially in adults",
 1159:     title: str = "Tirzepatide versus Semaglutide Once Weekly",
 1160:     journal: str = "New England Journal of Medicine",
 1161:     year: int = 2021,
 1162: ) -> dict[str, Any]:
 1163:     """Minimal OpenAlex /works/{doi} object with an
 1164:     abstract_inverted_index reconstructed from `sentence`."""
 1165:     inv: dict[str, list[int]] = {}
 1166:     for i, word in enumerate(sentence.split()):
 1167:         inv.setdefault(word, []).append(i)
 1168:     return {
 1169:         "doi": f"https://doi.org/{doi}",
 1170:         "title": title,
 1171:         "display_name": title,
 1172:         "publication_year": year,
 1173:         "authorships": [
 1174:             {"author": {"display_name": "Frias Juan P."}},
 1175:         ],
 1176:         "primary_location": {"source": {"display_name": journal}},
 1177:         "abstract_inverted_index": inv,
 1178:     }

 1253: def _collect_identifiers(binding: EvidenceBinding) -> dict[str, str]:
 1254:     """Flatten primary + secondary identifiers into a {kind: value}
 1255:     dict. Kinds: 'doi', 'pmid', 'url', 'anchor'."""
 1256:     out: dict[str, str] = {}
 1257:     for ident in (binding.primary_identifier, *binding.secondary_identifiers):
 1258:         if ":" not in ident:
 1259:             continue
 1260:         kind, value = ident.split(":", 1)
 1261:         out.setdefault(kind, value)
 1262:     return out
 1263:

  164: 
  165: class _Transport:
  166:     """Programmable httpx transport that returns canned responses by
  167:     URL substring match. Used to test the orchestrator without real
  168:     network."""
  169: 
  170:     def __init__(self, rules: list[tuple[str, int, Any]]) -> None:
  171:         """rules: list of (url_substring, status_code, body) tuples.
  172:         body can be dict (JSON) or str (text)."""
  173:         self.rules = rules
  174:         self.call_log: list[str] = []
  175: 
  176:     def __call__(self, request: httpx.Request) -> httpx.Response:
  177:         url = str(request.url)
  178:         self.call_log.append(url)
  179:         for sub, status, body in self.rules:
  180:             if sub in url:
  181:                 if isinstance(body, dict):
  182:                     return httpx.Response(status, json=body)
  183:                 if isinstance(body, str):
  184:                     return httpx.Response(
  185:                         status, text=body,
  186:                         headers={"content-type": "text/xml"},
  187:                     )
  188:                 return httpx.Response(status)
  189:         return httpx.Response(404, json={"error": "no_rule_matched"})
  190: 
  191: 
  192: class _SequencedTransport:
  193:     """Transport that returns different responses on successive calls
  194:     to the same URL substring. Used to exercise retry on transient
  195:     errors. `sequences[substring]` is consumed in FIFO order."""
  196: 
  197:     def __init__(self, sequences: dict[str, list[tuple[int, Any]]]) -> None:
  198:         self.sequences = {k: list(v) for k, v in sequences.items()}
  199:         self.call_log: list[str] = []
  200: 
  201:     def __call__(self, request: httpx.Request) -> httpx.Response:
  202:         url = str(request.url)
  203:         self.call_log.append(url)
  204:         for sub, seq in self.sequences.items():
  205:             if sub in url and seq:
  206:                 status, body = seq.pop(0)
  207:                 if isinstance(body, dict):
  208:                     return httpx.Response(status, json=body)
  209:                 if isinstance(body, str):
  210:                     return httpx.Response(
  211:                         status, text=body,
  212:                         headers={"content-type": "text/xml"},
  213:                     )
  214:                 return httpx.Response(status)
  215:         return httpx.Response(404, json={"error": "no_rule_matched"})
  216: 
  217: 
  218: def _client_with_transport(transport_fn: _Transport) -> httpx.Client:
  219:     return httpx.Client(
  220:         transport=httpx.MockTransport(transport_fn),
  221:         timeout=5.0,
  222:     )
  223: 
  224:

  441: class TestOrchestratorDoiConsistencyGuard:
  442:     """V30 Phase-2 run-1 root cause: contract had wrong PMID bound
  443:     to SURPASS-2 (actually SPRINT). NEJM blocked the DOI fetch,
  444:     M-56 fell back to PubMed, PubMed returned SPRINT abstract,
  445:     M-58 extracted wrong-paper content that passed anti-fabrication
  446:     (prose was verbatim in direct_quote). The guard rejects PubMed

 succeeded in 1195ms:
    2: 
    3: V30 Report Contract Architecture Layer 2b. Replaces Serper/S2
    4: non-deterministic keyword retrieval for known-identifier entities
    5: with three deterministic, free, never-paywalled APIs:
    6: 
    7:   1. CrossRef `/works/{doi}` — metadata (title, authors, abstract, year)
    8:   2. Unpaywall `/v2/{doi}`   — OA PDF URL if an OA version exists
    9:   3. PubMed EFetch (pmid)    — deterministic abstract XML when
   10:                                 full-text paywalled.
   11: 
   12: V28/V29 showed that keyword retrieval via Serper/S2 was the primary
   13: cause of V30 Defect A (non-determinism). Same M-48 variant queries
   14: landed different primary sets across runs. M-56 bypasses keyword
   15: retrieval entirely for known-DOI entities — given the same DOI the
   16: retriever emits a byte-identical FrameRow.
   17: 
   18: ## Layered architecture
   19: 
   20: The module has four distinct layers. Tests exercise them separately
   21: to isolate network dependency:
   22: 
   23:   Layer 1: Pure data types (FrameRow, ProvenanceClass, RetrievalAttempt).
   24:   Layer 2: Pure parsers (_parse_crossref_response, _parse_unpaywall_response,
   25:            _parse_pubmed_xml). Given raw API response, return structured
   26:            fields.
   27:   Layer 3: Network callers (_call_crossref, _call_unpaywall, _call_pubmed)
   28:            with bounded retry + fixed timeout + status-code-to-outcome
   29:            mapping.
   30:   Layer 4: Orchestrator (fetch_frame_entity) which dispatches by
   31:            primary_identifier and composes FrameRow.
   32: 
   33: ## Dependency injection for testability
   34: 
   35: `fetch_frame_entity(binding, *, client=None, ...)` accepts an
   36: optional httpx.Client. Production callers pass None (module creates
   37: one per call); tests pass a fake client that returns canned
   38: responses. No test needs monkey-patching of module globals.
   39: 
   40: ## Codex V30 plan pass-1 revision #4 (M-60 manifest metadata)
   41: 
   42: Every fetch attempt — success or failure — is logged into
   43: FrameRow.retrieval_attempts: list of RetrievalAttempt(source, url,
   44: status, duration_ms, outcome). M-60 manifest rendering consumes this
   45: log to explain exactly what the pipeline tried for every slot that
   46: ended up in frame_gap_unrecoverable state.
   47: 
   48: ## Determinism contract
   49: 
   50: Given the same (binding, same upstream API responses), the same
   51: FrameRow is emitted. Specifically:
   52:   - No wall-clock reads other than duration measurement (which is
   53:     logged but does not affect the FrameRow payload proper).
   54:   - No randomness in retry backoff (fixed 1s/2s/4s schedule).
   55:   - Sort order within parsed fields is explicit.
   56:   - direct_quote is deterministic given inputs.

   78: class ProvenanceClass(str, Enum):
   79:     """Provenance of the content captured in FrameRow.direct_quote.
   80: 
   81:     open_access: full OA text retrieved (preferred; richest for M-58
   82:       slot-fill).
